<td style="text-align:center;"><strong class="selflink">men</strong>  <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Women's tournament">women</a></td>

</tr>

<p>The <b><a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics">men's football tournament</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a></b> was held in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and five other cities in Great Britain from 26 July to 11 August. Associations affiliated with <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> were invited to enter their men's U-23 teams in regional qualifying competitions, from which 15 teams, plus the hosts <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Olympic_football_team" title="Great Britain Olympic football team">Great Britain</a>, reached the final tournament. Men's teams were allowed to augment their squads with three players over the age of 23. It was the first major <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>-organised men's tournament to be held within the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> since the <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966 FIFA World Cup</a> and was the first men's Olympic football tournament to feature a team representing <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Olympic_football_team" title="Great Britain Olympic football team">Great Britain</a> since the <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Olympics" title="1960 Summer Olympics">1960 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIFA_regulations_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIFA_regulations-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The gold medal was won by <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_under-23_football_team" title="Mexico national under-23 football team">Mexico</a> who defeated Brazil 2–1 in the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualifying">Qualifying</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Qualifying">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Each <a href="/wiki/National_Olympic_Committee" title="National Olympic Committee">National Olympic Committee</a> may enter one men's team in the football tournament.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Squads">Squads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Squads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_team_squads" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's team squads">Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's team squads</a></div>
<p>For the men's tournament, each nation submitted a squad of 18 players, 15 of whom had to be born on or after 1 January 1989, and three of whom could be overage players. A minimum of two goalkeepers (plus one optional alternate goalkeeper) had to be included in the squad.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Match_officials">Match officials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Match officials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Draw">Draw</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Draw">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The draw for the tournament took place on 24 April 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Great Britain, Mexico, Brazil and Spain were seeded for the draw and placed into groups A–D, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The remaining teams were drawn from four pots with teams from the same region kept apart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Preliminary_round">Preliminary round</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Preliminary round">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Group winners and runners-up advanced to the quarter-finals (also see <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics#Tie_breakers" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics">Tie breakers</a>).</p>
<p><small>All times are <a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">British Summer Time</a> (<a href="/wiki/UTC%2B01:00" title="UTC+01:00">UTC+1</a>).</small></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quarter-finals">Quarter-finals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Quarter-finals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="vevent" style="width: 100%; background-color: {{{bgc}}}; clear:both">
<p><span class="summary" style="display: none;"><a href="/wiki/Japan_national_under-23_football_team" title="Japan national under-23 football team">Japan</a><span class="flagicon"> <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/23px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/35px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Flag_of_Japan.svg/45px-Flag_of_Japan.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></span> v <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/23px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/35px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Flag_of_Egypt.svg/45px-Flag_of_Egypt.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_under-23_football_team" title="Egypt national under-23 football team">Egypt</a></span></p>

<td>
<div style="text-align:right">4 August 2012<br/>
12:00<br/>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Goalscorers">Goalscorers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Goalscorers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With six goals, Leandro Damião of Brazil is the top scorer in the tournament. In total, 76 goals were scored by 49 different players, with none of them credited as own goal.</p>
<dl>
<dt>6 goals</dt>
</dl>

<dl>
<dt>Red cards</dt>
</dl>
<div>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;">
<tr>
<td style="width: 33.33%;text-align:left;vertical-align:top;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Controversies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Queues">Queues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Queues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Controversies_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Controversies at the 2012 Summer Olympics">Controversies at the 2012 Summer Olympics</a></div>
<p>For the first matchday at <a href="/wiki/St_James%27_Park" title="St James' Park">St James' Park</a>, there were long queues at the box office, leading to fans missing some of the game. A spokesman for Ticketmaster said: "We saw extremely high numbers of spectators arriving at St James' Park to purchase football tickets on the day of the event. While Ticketmaster is contracted to manage the box offices at Olympic venues, the staff numbers at those venues are determined by LOCOG. We will continue to work closely with LOCOG to ensure that the box office staff levels are sufficient to meet the demands for ticket sales and collection". LOCOG described the situation as "totally and completely 100% unacceptable", and after changes were made in the process, the issue was reportedly avoided for the second round of matches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the matches held at the <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> on 29 July, fans were subjected to long queues at the <a href="/wiki/Concession_stand" title="Concession stand">concession stands</a> in the ground after <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a>'s card payment system crashed, leaving cash payment as the only alternative. The situation was compounded by the fact that, as Visa had been granted exclusive rights to the Olympics, other cards could not be accepted as payment, and the number of <a href="/wiki/Automated_teller_machine" title="Automated teller machine">cash machines</a> in the stadium had been reduced after 27 that worked on the <a href="/wiki/LINK_(UK)" title="LINK (UK)">LINK</a> system had been removed to be replaced by eight that could only be used by Visa cards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>There were several problems relating to transport for events held at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>. There was severe congestion at <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Central_railway_station" title="Cardiff Central railway station">Cardiff Central railway station</a> when <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Olympic_football_team" title="Great Britain Olympic football team">Great Britain</a> played South Korea;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and the bronze medal match also had rail disruption when a retaining wall collapsed onto the tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Player_sent_home">Player sent home</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Player sent home">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Swiss footballer <a href="/wiki/Michel_Morganella" title="Michel Morganella">Michel Morganella</a> was sent home by the <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_under-23_football_team" title="Switzerland national under-23 football team">Switzerland team</a> following their <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament_%E2%80%93_Group_B#South_Korea_vs_Switzerland" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament – Group B">2–1 loss against South Korea</a> after he sent a tweet that, according to the director of Swiss Olympic Committee Gian Gilli, "discriminated, insulted and violated the dignity of the South Korean football team and people".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Britain_football_teams">Great Britain football teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Great Britain football teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the criticism against Scottish female player <a href="/wiki/Kim_Little" title="Kim Little">Kim Little</a>, for choosing not to sing the British national anthem "<a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen" title="God Save the Queen">God Save the Queen</a>" because of her national identity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> other Scottish and Welsh players, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Bellamy" title="Craig Bellamy">Craig Bellamy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ifeoma_Dieke" title="Ifeoma Dieke">Ifeoma Dieke</a>, also attracted comment in the media for remaining silent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph-anthem_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-anthem-51">[51]</a></sup> Giggs, the Great Britain men's captain, later said: "The problem is the British anthem is the same as the English anthem and if you're a Welshman or a Scotsman it's difficult".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Organising_Committee_of_the_Olympic_Games_and_Paralympic_Games" title="London Organising Committee of the Olympic Games and Paralympic Games">LOCOG</a> also apologised after an error in the official match programme for the first game mistakenly described Welsh player <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joe_Allen_(footballer_born_1990)" title="Joe Allen (footballer born 1990)">Joe Allen</a> as being English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_statement_made_by_Park_Jong-woo">Political statement made by Park Jong-woo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Political statement made by Park Jong-woo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/South_Korea_national_under-23_football_team" title="South Korea national under-23 football team">South Korea</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_under-23_football_team" title="Japan national under-23 football team">Japan</a> in the bronze medal match at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> on 10 August, South Korean player <a href="/wiki/Park_Jong-woo" title="Park Jong-woo">Park Jong-woo</a> walked around the field holding a banner with a political message written in Korean, "독도는 우리 땅!" (<i>dokdo neun uri ttang</i>, lit.: "<a href="/wiki/Liancourt_Rocks" title="Liancourt Rocks">Dokdo</a> is our territory").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> This incident occurred on the same night after South Korean President <a href="/wiki/Lee_Myung-bak" title="Lee Myung-bak">Lee Myung-bak</a> had visited the islands which both South Korea and Japan claim as their territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The IOC and FIFA reviewed the evidence, since FIFA statutes prohibit political statements being made by athletes at Olympic events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The IOC barred Park from the bronze medal ceremony and did not permit him to receive his medal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In addition, it asked FIFA to discipline Park, and stated that it may decide on further sanctions at a later date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> IOC president <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Rogge" title="Jacques Rogge">Jacques Rogge</a> told reporters: "We will take a possible decision of what will happen with the medal later".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> FIFA failed to reach a conclusion on the case at a meeting at its Zürich headquarters held on 5 October, and the disciplinary committee discussed the case again on the following week,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> then again failed to reach a verdict. After that, the Korean Olympic Committee (KOC) announced that Park would receive his bronze medal. The case was heard again by the committee on 20 November,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> and FIFA finally decided and announced on 3 December to suspend Park for two matches after he was considered to have breached the FIFA Disciplinary Code and the Regulations of the Olympic Football Tournaments. FIFA also imposed a warning on the Korea Football Association and reminded it of its obligation to properly instruct its players on all the pertinent rules and applicable regulations before the start of any competition, in order to avoid such incidents in the future. The Korea Football Association was warned that should incidents of such nature occur again in the future, the FIFA Disciplinary Committee may impose harsher sanctions on the Korea Football Association.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
